<div id="review_267463727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267463727" />
    <a title="Sofija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4452470-sofija"><img alt="Sofija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287851381p2/4452470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267463727?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofija" href="/user/show/4452470-sofija">Sofija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13100412-poughkeepsie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4452470-sofija?shelf=couldn-t-finished">couldn-t-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267463727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11357213181805052167">I should have listened to my friends when they advised me against reading “Poughkeepsie”. But I was interested in the idea of a girl falling for a homeless guy, so I decided to read it anyway.<br/>From the beginning I was overwhelmed with the cheesy lines. Livia behaved like and adolescent and Blake didn’t stir up any emotions except for pity. It is said that from hate to love is only one step, but I think that for women from pity to love is 1/3 of this step. It’s in our DNA for some bizarre reason. </span>
  <span id="freeText11357213181805052167" style="display:none">I should have listened to my friends when they advised me against reading “Poughkeepsie”. But I was interested in the idea of a girl falling for a homeless guy, so I decided to read it anyway.<br>From the beginning I was overwhelmed with the cheesy lines. Livia behaved like and adolescent and Blake didn’t stir up any emotions except for pity. It is said that from hate to love is only one step, but I think that for women from pity to love is 1/3 of this step. It’s in our DNA for some bizarre reason. So I understand why Livia fallen for him. But for me it was still hard to get into their relationship. I have certain image in my mind of the homeless people. Instead of seeing this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368240i/720792.jpg" width="183" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368240i/720793.jpg" width="512" height="341" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I kept seeing this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368240i/720794._SX540_.jpg" width="640" height="341" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368240i/720795._SX540_.jpg" width="640" height="341" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So every time Livia kissed the guy instead of thinking “It’s so romantic!” I thought: “Yack! It’s so insanitary!”. <br><br><i>"She put a sweet kiss in the center of his palm"</i><br> <br>He is homeless!!! How often does she think he washes his hands?<br> <br>I also kept wondering why Blake couldn’t find a work. Yes, he has problems with being in the sun, but there are a lot of works that need to be done at night. So apparently he doesn’t want to work which means that he is ether lazy or given up on life, which make him weak and not attractive as main male protagonist.<br><br>And I didn’t like Livia too. Author was trying so hard to make her look ideal and to show us that her moral principles are so much better that other people because she helped homeless guy while they ignored him. But sometimes she was just mean. For example:<br><br><i>Another commuter stepped out from behind Livia and asked, “Is this piece of trash bothering you, lady?” Livia suppressed the need to punch the guy in the stomach.</i><br><br>This guy tried to help her because he was concerned for her safety and she acted so ungrateful. <br>Or when she talks to her boyfriend and humiliates him and generally treats him like dirt.<br><br><i>“Nope. Dave’s right. I kissed another man. And he kissed the hell out of me. I think I’m still aroused from the whole incident.” Livia watched rage crawl up Chris’s arms and tense his face.</i><br><br>Yes, she is such sensitive and compassionate person.<br><br>The boyfriend is not an angel himself, but she didn’t know it at the time. And while she thought some mean stuff about him I wondered why did she dated him then? She accepted his marriage proposal knowing that she wouldn’t marry him. She also threw away her engagement ring. He did by this ring even if there was a fake diamond. Livia could returned it back to him or not accept it in the first place.<br><br>And then suddenly the POVs attack started. There were three friends, their three love interests and plus evil ex-boyfriend and so total seven POVs. It was like reading three different books being reshuffled all the time. <br><br>But the main drawback was that the writing was so melodramatic and exaggerating. The ex-boyfriend is SUPER MEGA DUCHEBAG. He is sleeping with other girls, he has lame friends, loves his car more than anything. His work is to kill defenseless deers by shooting them in the head and he likes it. He literally wet his pants once when being threatened by a girl. <br>One of the Blake friends is SUPER MEGA GANGSTER. He uses drugs, kills people right and left, his residency is in some abandon house in the worst neighborhood, and he controls the quality of hookers himself with some help of Viagra. But despite all this he has a gentle soul. <br><br>And the same is with all the other characters. Entire book is an overstatement. And because of this, characters seems two dimensional and a little bit caricaturistic.<br> <br>I’ve read the half of it before I understand that this book and I wasn't meant for each other.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11357213181805052167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Amazing <br/>The story... Exceptional <br/>The relationship between the 6 main characters?!..</span>
  <span id="freeText1683689874941705000" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> "He counts. You've smiled at him four hundred and forty six times as of a few minutes ago. He announces the number every time I see him." - Cole </i>
</b><br /><br />What a <b>FAN-FUCKING-TASTIC</b> read. <br />Seriously I don't think I can describe how much I loved this book. I literally devoured it! <br /><br />Who knew that all it would take is a smile and you can change someone life? <br />The characters.. Phenomenal! <br />The brotherhood between the 3 boys... Amazing <br />The story... Exceptional <br />The relationship between the 6 main characters?!... Beautiful <br />The love between Blake and Livia.... Electrifying! <br /><br />Livia catches the train everyday to school. Everyday she makes sure to smile at the others on the platform. She always smiles at the homeless man sitting in the shadows as well. She calls him "Green Eyes." One morning while waiting for the train a group of teens start to pick on him. She stands up for him and shoo's them away. <br />That's the first time they talk. <br />She realizes he's beautiful and they make introductions. <br />The story is whirlwind from there. <br /><br /><br />Cole, Blake and Beckett are brothers. Not by blood, but that doesn't matter they are brothers in the only way that matters their hearts. <br />Cole is going to become a priest. <br />Beckett is lord of the crime world. <br />Blake is homeless. <br />These brothers would do <b>ANYTHING</b> for each other. <br /><br />Livia and Kyle are sisters. Complete opposites. <br />Eve well she has a back story that you need to read to know about, as I'm not spoiling it. <br /><br />These 6 characters makes up this beautiful book. I will also mention Mouse as well. He is not part of the foster care relationship with Blake, Cole and Beckett but he does play a big role. <br />Their relationships are tried and tested. Hearts laid on the line. Bad things done. Horrible things are done.Good things done. Great things done. <br />It does have a dark side though. The second half of the book does get very dark but I still loved it. <br /><br />I loved all the endings that everyone got, I would of liked to know a bit more about Beckett's but I'm not complaining. <br /><br />Sometimes the things that Beckett and Kyle said were hilarious! so it broke up some of the darkness of this emotional read.<br /><br />I really am glad that I read this book. A few GR friends have read this and didn't like it and as we have the same tastes I was a bit worried about it, but still decided to read it anyway. I've never been so happy. Seriously think this is my new Favorite book! <br /><br />Some of my favorite parts were- <br /><br />"I can't leave." Green Eyes took a huge breath. "This is the only place where I get to see you." -Blake<br />.................<br />"Do you have to park on the lawn every time?" Cole asked. <br />"The government's beating us down, it all begins with those goddamn lines in the parking lot. Set yourself free, my brother. If you see a line, ignore it." -Beckett <br />.................<br />"Livia, you make the rest of the beautiful things in the world cry for even trying at all. You make it hard for me to breathe." - Blake <br />.................<br />Eve had just fucked his mind so hard, he wanted to smoke a cigarette and cuddle like some soap watching woman. - Beckett <br />.................<br />"Correction- my pussy smells like a monkey that got fucked by a dirty gorilla. Did I shower last night?" - Kyle <br />................<br />"Hey, monkey pussy, you might want to give those meat curtains a spit shine before you leave the house." Mouse pointed to Kyle's crotch with a knitting needle. Mouse looked around in the stunned silence. "What? I knit, but I'm still hardcore.Seriously."<br /> Kyle swore-muttered something about "talking about my dick mitten in the middle of my own goddamn kitchen," and stomped upstairs. <br />................<br />"I'm pissing straight alcohol," Kyle informed from above. "Still peeing...still peeing...Oh GOD, I'm bladdertastic!" - Kyle <br />................<br />"We don't wear rings because we like to fuck other people too." The geriatric nurse blushed deeply as Beckett gave her a once over. "Don't be shy, baby, I'm not afraid of Senior lovin'." - Beckett<br />................<br />"Holy fucking dogs! You scared the uterus out of me!" - Kyle <br />................<br />"Beckett is all sorts of bad because of what he does, but who he is- that's very beautiful." - Livia <br />...............<br />"Beckett is probably the hardest person there is to love, he does life wrong for all the right reasons." - Blake <br />..............<br />"Everytime I think i couldn't love you a bit more, you stretch my heart again" - Livia <br />..............<br />"Blake, Cole and I have been family for each other, because the ones we started with were for crap. Why they let me in, I still don't know. But because they did, I believed I was worth more than I would otherwise." <br /> "Blake's company made me want to hug trees and hear music. Cole's company made me want to try harder to be a better person. I never imagined that anyone could love either of these men enough for me to let them go."<br /> "But I didn't know the McHugh girls. Their love is fiercer than guns. More powerful than fistfuls of money. I can walk away because of them." Beckett held his glass high. "To my brothers. They have finally gotton the lives they deserve." <br /></span>

<div id="review_650797221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650797221" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12059859-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576765878p2/12059859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650797221?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/12059859-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=mental-issues">mental-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=reclusive-guys">reclusive-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=absolute-faves">absolute-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=cried-like-a-little-bitch">cried-like-a-little-bitch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=profound-meaning">profound-meaning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=6-stars-of-above-and-beyond-awesome">6-stars-of-above-and-beyond-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650797221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1219343241148718191"><b>
  <i> 6 Magical Stars!!! </i>
</b><br/><br/><i> Fave book of January 2014!</i><br/><br/>Would you ever give a homeless person a chance? Not a dollar, or a meal....a chance. Would you? Would you ever look at them an equal? Well, Livia does just that. She sees Blake every day and smiles at him like she would anyone else. She doesn't realize that these mere smiles are the peak of his day. <i>Poughkeepsie</i> is an amazing story about appearances not being what they seem, about life, about struggle, love, and pain. Blake is troubled and might</span>
  <span id="freeText1219343241148718191" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> 6 Magical Stars!!! </i>
</b><br><br><i> Fave book of January 2014!</i><br><br>Would you ever give a homeless person a chance? Not a dollar, or a meal....a chance. Would you? Would you ever look at them an equal? Well, Livia does just that. She sees Blake every day and smiles at him like she would anyone else. She doesn't realize that these mere smiles are the peak of his day. <i>Poughkeepsie</i> is an amazing story about appearances not being what they seem, about life, about struggle, love, and pain. Blake is troubled and might be perceived as ugly on the outside, because of his current state. However, Chris, Livia's current boyfriend is beautiful on the outside but is disgusting on the inside. But no one around her sees these things. They only see what's on the surface. Blake and Livia meet and form a friendship that slowly begins to evolve into more, until they fall madly, passionately, soul-changingly in love with each other. <br><br><b>
  <i> "You let me touch you. Kiss you. Your skin? It feels like piano keys. My hands know just where to go." ~Blake<br><br>"I feel like I've always loved him, and now I just got lucky enough to find him." ~Livia</i>
</b><br><br>Man oh man! What to say.... I have really been putting off writing this review because there is no way that my words will even come close to doing this book justice. I beyond loved it! This was a game changer, the bar raiser, I fell in love with the words, the characters, and the beautiful story. <br><br>I have read some pretty great books lately, but <i> Poughkeepsie</i> is one of those books that is just, in a league of its own! <br><br>I had heard that the story was a love story about a homeless man who forms a relationship with a kind girl that he meets at the train station. The blurb captured me instantly, and it would have been enough. But in actuality, this story is about soooo much more! It's really about three blood brothers with less than fortunate childhoods, who met in foster care and made a pact. They knew they couldn't trust their surroundings, but they could trust each other. They are all that they have. And they each find a different way to deal with their circumstances. <br><br>Blake is one of the brothers, and the book is mainly about him, however, the stories of his two brothers Cole and Beckett are very tightly intertwined into the book. So you do have multiple story lines going on at once. I read some reviews where people felt that there were too many story lines going on and that it left them not being able to connect to the main characters. I really couldn't disagree more. Each of the stories are beautifully written and absolutely kept me captivated the entire time. And in the end, all of the story lines come together beautifully. <br><br>Now, let's talk about the writing. This was the first time I read Debra Anastasia's writing and let me tell you...WOW!! Her prose honestly reminds me of Sylvain Reynard's who is my GOD, in case you are not aware!! It has an almost poetic quality to it. She builds characters with such humanity that you feel like you can reach out and touch them. Her words have such a beautiful tenderness to them that by about 8% into this book, I felt 100% invested!! <br><br>That's really all there is to say. I cannot recommend this book highly enough. It has now become one of my very favorite series and I cannot wait for more!!<br><br><b>Castings:</b><br><a href="http://s996.photobucket.com/user/Vanessa_RB-Babe/media/63c68723-e884-44e7-9699-b5c6bdad5035_zps3e5ddf74.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389984378i/8119839._SY540_.png" alt=" photo 63c68723-e884-44e7-9699-b5c6bdad5035_zps3e5ddf74.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><a href="http://s996.photobucket.com/user/Vanessa_RB-Babe/media/1119bf46-be26-43e8-9a3c-8bcc6c6d580e_zps358161f9.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389984378i/8119840._SX540_.png" alt=" photo 1119bf46-be26-43e8-9a3c-8bcc6c6d580e_zps358161f9.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“He kept his head down in what seemed to be a prayer. “He counts. You've smiled at him four hundred and forty-six times as of a few minutes ago. He announces the number every time I see him.” ~Cole </i>
</b><br></span>

<div id="review_253117668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253117668" />
    <a title="Kajal Nehra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7253942-kajal-nehra"><img alt="Kajal Nehra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576629088p2/7253942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253117668?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kajal Nehra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kajal Nehra" href="/user/show/7253942-kajal-nehra">Kajal Nehra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253942-kajal-nehra?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253942-kajal-nehra?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253942-kajal-nehra?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253117668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12215821978066083622"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>"Blake doesn't ask her for money. He doesn't know her name. All he wants to do is... count her smiles."</b><br/><br/>The book was all the things I wanted to read. I can't be any happier to say that I'm glad I picked it up. I saw the trailer video first and just halfway through the video I was teary-eyed! :P<br/>Poughkeepsie is surely one of my favorites, because:<br/><br/>- It is a very <b>unique</b> novel. There are books which follow the same old story line and just change the characters, but Poughkeepsie was something </span>
  <span id="freeText12215821978066083622" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><b>"Blake doesn't ask her for money. He doesn't know her name. All he wants to do is... count her smiles."</b><br /><br />The book was all the things I wanted to read. I can't be any happier to say that I'm glad I picked it up. I saw the trailer video first and just halfway through the video I was teary-eyed! :P<br />Poughkeepsie is surely one of my favorites, because:<br /><br />- It is a very <b>unique</b> novel. There are books which follow the same old story line and just change the characters, but Poughkeepsie was something very new that I just fell in love with.<br /><br />- Blake is the perfect example for a gentleman, and I don't know but I'm a little biased when it comes to gentlemen. Not my fault, there just aren't enough chivalrous men anymore! :D<br /><br />- <b>Beckett</b>, oh Beckett! God where do I start? He is the perfect bastard! The best. And I'd be lying if I said I didn't just fall in love with him. <i>*faints*</i><br />He was like a mother trying to protect her children from all the harms that could come to them. Like a protective father, he could kick anyone's ass who ever dreamed of harming his brothers. The way he loved Livia and Kyle, and how selflessly he left Eve just so she could spread her wings, takes me on a crying spree again and again. I have utmost respect for this fucker!<br /><i>He fucking ruled the book!</i><br /> <br />- Livia is the bravest woman I've ever seen :) I loved her character and personality more than any of the other female protagonists I've ever loved.<br /><br />- John. He is the best father I could imagine. Not those fake ones we see in our books these days, but a very real one! Maybe because even my father is a single parent to me I can understand and relate to him better, but either way, he gained my respect in every fatherly aspect.<br /><br />- <b>Kyle</b> I can most relate to, I guess. When I read about her, it was like I was reading about myself. Not the parts where she goes on fucking guys and all, but except that all those other parts. I mean it: each and every scene. Even her story superimposes mine so perfectly that I cry every time I think about it. I just hope my story also ends just as beautifully as hers did.<br /><br />- Mouse was one character who made me laugh a lot. All the squeaky voice and body-builder physique. :D But after I read his story, it sucks so bad that Debra did what she did to him! :'( I'm putting all the blame on you, Debra. Because you know that it wasn't fair! :'(<br /><br />- Chris, was the worst motherfucker I've ever seen! God, I'm so proud of Debra and Beckett that they killed him! GO BECKETT! GO DEBRA! Wohooo! ;D<br /><br />- Eve rocked big time! I'd love to learn all those things she can do. Someday. :P<br /><br />- Thanks to Becektt I now know like a dozen new swear words! God, Debra I love you and your creativity! <i>*salutes*</i><br /><br />- And lastly, this book introduced me to Ron Pope!!! Wow. I'm a fan now. I simply fell in love with his music. :')<br /><br /><i>Don't get me wrong, it was everything a 5-starer should be, BUT my boy didn't get his Happily Ever After, and so I have all the rights to deduct half-a-star for that.</i> :'(<br /><br /><b>Note to author</b>: We want a novella! A Beckett and Eve's happily ever after. Please? Otherwise I'll cry. Seriously. :'( :'(<br />After everything that he did, he sure as fucking hell doesn't deserve a hanging/unknown ending. This is not done.<br /><br />POUGHKEEPSIE TOOK MY BREATH AWAY! IT IS SURELY ONE OF MY BEST READS FOR 2012! I know its kinda early to say that, but try all that you can but you can't make me say that its not one of my favorites! I bet ya! ;) :D<br /><br />Go go go! Wait no more, because you're missing out on such a <b>BEAUTIFUL, WONDERFUL, UNIQUE, HEART-TOUCHING, AROUSING</b> (and lord everything else!) book! :))</span>
  <a data-text-id="12215821978066083622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240598812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240598812" />
    <a title="Margarida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3005178-margarida"><img alt="Margarida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579386125p2/3005178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240598812?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margarida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margarida" href="/user/show/3005178-margarida">Margarida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3005178-margarida?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3005178-margarida?shelf=didnt-finish">didnt-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240598812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6617448425834486207">Wow...not at all what I was expecting. I mean this in a bad way, obviously. Not a thing in this book seemed realistic to me. The characters weren't complex, instead they were predictable, silly, unlikeable and everything about them screamed "stereotype me". It's a pity, because I really wanted to like this book. I heard so many wonderful things about it. Now the only thing that's crossing my mind is how can people find this beautiful, romantic and well-written? It's cheesy, creepy and lacks dept</span>
  <span id="freeText6617448425834486207" style="display:none">Wow...not at all what I was expecting. I mean this in a bad way, obviously. Not a thing in this book seemed realistic to me. The characters weren't complex, instead they were predictable, silly, unlikeable and everything about them screamed "stereotype me". It's a pity, because I really wanted to like this book. I heard so many wonderful things about it. Now the only thing that's crossing my mind is how can people find this beautiful, romantic and well-written? It's cheesy, creepy and lacks depth, complexity and passion. Anyway, awesome that you liked, really. Not criticizing anyone here, just sharing my opinion.<br /><br />Back to my review...I didn't really felt any love between them, it all seemed so sudden and the chemistry between the two was non-existant. They were so boring together and maybe I missed something, but Livia seemed to all of a sudden realize she was in love with Blake. And she kissed him. While she still dated Chris. Where are your morals now, huh? Not so perfect anymore now are you? Why the heck did Livia date Chris for years, in the first place, if she didn't felt annything towards him? In fact, it seemed she truly despised him. He used to talk to his friends about her, in her presence, saying 'her face is nothing special but the ass is rockin' (or something like this). LOL. You need more self-respect, Livia!<br /><br />I'm pretty pissed off that she's a psychology major btw...being one myself, I never would've dealt with Blake the way she did. Maybe she's just too stupid. Let's start with the fact that he's a complete stranger and she still hands him her car keys. I mean, who lets a homeless stranger man lead them to their car, at night, and actually hands him the keys? I know I wouldn't. She doesn't know him and he's homeless. As hot as the guy is, he's homeless and a stranger. She doesn't know a thing about him. <br /><br /> <br />Blake was as annoying as Livia, really, if not more. Oay, I didn't read the whole book (I tried, hoping that it would get better, but when it only got worse, I decided to stop) but the guy was a total jerk and extremly proud. Let's be honest here, what homeless super-hungry guy wouldn't accept food because he thought he didn't 'earn' it? Seriously? Someone is kindly offering him food and he rejects, saying that he would only eat the damn sandwich if Livia offered one to the other people around them, waiting for the train (more than 50 people). And you know what? She does that the next day! LOL. She gives a sandwich to more than 50 people so Blake accepts one too. This happens a little after they talk for the first time, and as I read this stupidity I got the feeling that maybe this book wasn't for me, but I decided to give it a chance, anyway.<br /><br />Kyle has mommy issues (cliche?) and her first meeting with Cole was so...I don't even have a word for it. LOL. WTH.<br /><br />So, so disappointed with this book. I really thought I'd like it after the inumerous people who recc'd it to me while it still was a twilight fanfiction. :( It's full of clichés and cheesy/lame phrases that made me throw up a little in my mouth. And it lack one very important thing in romance books: passions, intensity, chemistry. I felt like they were two boring people who claimed to be in love but didn't know a thing about what that means. The author should've edited and improved her work, it seems underworked and full of faults to me.<br /></span>

<div id="review_239561606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239561606" />
    <a title="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog"><img alt="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416791332p2/4597644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239561606?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog" href="/user/show/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog">Tessamari ♥Many Waters...♥ ~ Sweet Spot Book Blog</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13100412-poughkeepsie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=crack-books">crack-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4597644-tessamari-many-waters-sweet-spot-book-blog?shelf=highly-emotional">highly-emotional</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239561606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16838009906776632774">I'm giving this mother-effin book 5++ stars...like for real! LOL.<br/><br/>I'm not sure how to accurately review this book. Lets begin with, <b>I LOVED IT!!!</b>. Its such a rare treat to find a story that not only has you in tears, but also makes you giggle and laugh at the same time. This book had it all. Tons and tons of drama, heartache, laughter, violence, and lets not forget the explicit banter. Having a sailor mouth myself, I ate it all up and loved every minute of it. I felt the language just added more </span>
  <span id="freeText16838009906776632774" style="display:none">I'm giving this mother-effin book 5++ stars...like for real! LOL.<br><br>I'm not sure how to accurately review this book. Lets begin with, <b>I LOVED IT!!!</b>. Its such a rare treat to find a story that not only has you in tears, but also makes you giggle and laugh at the same time. This book had it all. Tons and tons of drama, heartache, laughter, violence, and lets not forget the explicit banter. Having a sailor mouth myself, I ate it all up and loved every minute of it. I felt the language just added more hidden beauty to the story. In addition to the multitude of explicit language, there were also plenty of gentleman-like talk to balance it all out. The story needed this balance, simply because the characters wouldn't have been the same without it. Speaking of characters, this story had a fantastic cast of characters, I adored all of them. They made me get absorbed in their story. We had the brothers, which consisted of Blake, Beckett and Cole, though towards the end, included Mouse :) Then there are the heroines: Livia &amp; Kyle McHugh and Eve.<br><br>&lt;&lt;&gt;&gt;<br><br><b>Blake &amp; Livia:</b> The story ultimately revolves around this couple. Blake is first and foremost a gentleman. He is sweet, kind, &amp; romantic. However, Blake is homeless and constantly struggles with his past wrongs. Livia is kind and believes everyone deserves a smile. Blake is captivated when Livia first smiles at him at the train station, his home. Ever since that first smile, he's been counting her smiles. Blake makes sure he is always there to receive Livia's smiles, before she boards the train and after she disembarks for the evening. The story of smile number two hundred and eighty six made me cry (you just have to read it to find out why). There are many roadblocks this couple has to go through to get their HEA, but it made for wonderful reading.<br><br><b>Beckett &amp; Eve:</b> This story could not be what it is without Beckett. I adore Beckett. Beckett knowingly sold his soul to the devil to make his brothers' lives easier. Beckett is a beautiful soul, though its far from obvious. He's a foul-mouthed gangster. He's a big-time pimp &amp; drug dealer. He does everything for his brothers. Blake, Beckett and Cole aren't related by blood, but the three are deeply connected to each other and are bonded by their horrible foster care experience. If you mess with his brothers, you will feel his wrath. Eve works for Beckett as his stealthy assassin. Beckett realizes that Eve's initial plan was to kill Beckett himself. Beckett unknowingly starts a series of misfortunes that ultimately resulted in Eve loosing her fiance and unborn baby. Though she's out for revenge, she just can't seal the deal, no matter how many times the opportunity presented itself. She finds herself falling for Beckett and vice versa. But is loving Beckett enough? And can Beckett live with her decision?<br><br><b>Cole &amp; Kyle:</b> Cole is a man of faith. Though he isn't a full pledged priest, he aspires to be one. He keeps his brothers grounded. He wants to save them. Kyle is Livia's baby sister. They are extremely close. Their banter borders on hilarity at times. She is hilarious. Her foul-mouth can give Beckett a run for his money. The things that come out of her mouth had me laughing. I love Kyle. However, Kyle has multiple issues, mostly involving her mother. She tries to placate her problems by sleeping around. While speaking with Livia, Kyle explained her need to sleep around and why Cole is different:<br><br><i>"Do you know how many guys I've been with?" Kyle asked, meeting her eyes for just a moment. "So many. You know why? Because in that moment, just before you let them f*** you, you're the center of their universe. It lasts just seconds, but I like that feeling. I crave that feeling."<br>"This morning-last night? Whenever it was, standing in the church in front of him? I had that feeling. I was the center of his universe. And we had all our clothes on. That feeling lasted for hours."</i><br><br>Ying and Yang. It was a great sub-plot reading about these two. <br><br><b>Mouse:</b> I just have to mention Mouse, because why not? I LOVE Mouse. He works as muscle for Beckett. He is big, he's bad, he's smart and fiercely loyal to Beckett. The kicker, he loves to knit. He was even knitting ski masks for their next bank job. I simply loved it. He made me laugh and he definitely made me cry. Love you Mouse :)<br><br>I apologize for the lengthy review, but it just had to be done. I'm sure I still missed a lot of what I wanted to say, but no matter what, I just can't do this book any justice. It was a wonderfully written story and I give HUGE props to the fabulous author for sharing it. I <b>HIGHLY</b> recommend! <br><br>-----<br><b><u>FOLLOW ME</u></b><br><a href="http://s1094.photobucket.com/user/thessamari/media/Banner2_zps7a6c719e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379801013i/678281.jpg" alt=" photo Banner2_zps7a6c719e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><b>Blog:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sweetspotbookblog.com">www.sweetspotbookblog.com</a><br><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/SweetSpotBookBlog">www.facebook.com/SweetSpotBookBlog</a><br><b>Twitter:</b>@thessamari</span>
  <a data-text-id="16838009906776632774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_863776335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863776335" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6049062-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460575899p2/6049062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863776335?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/6049062-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13100412-poughkeepsie">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jen by: </span>
      steph
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=buddy-read-with-books-n-buddies">buddy-read-with-books-n-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=dark-reads">dark-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=new-adult-dark-contemporary">new-adult-dark-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=buddy-read-with-steph">buddy-read-with-steph</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=kindle-own">kindle-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=damaged-hero-heroine">damaged-hero-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=march-reads">march-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863776335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10915719405029360107">I don't even know where to start with this review. I suppose I will start by saying that I loved every page, every word in this story. It ticked all of my boxes for what I enjoy in an entertaining story. It had romance, sex,violence,humor,frienship,loyalty,and the biggest theme; family. When I began this book, I expected a love story about a homeless boy named Blake Hartt, and a girl from a middle class family that comes across Blake on her way to school each day at the underground train station</span>
  <span id="freeText10915719405029360107" style="display:none">I don't even know where to start with this review. I suppose I will start by saying that I loved every page, every word in this story. It ticked all of my boxes for what I enjoy in an entertaining story. It had romance, sex,violence,humor,frienship,loyalty,and the biggest theme; family. When I began this book, I expected a love story about a homeless boy named Blake Hartt, and a girl from a middle class family that comes across Blake on her way to school each day at the underground train station:Livia McHugh. Don't get me wrong, this book WAS about their beautiful journey into falling in love; but it was so much MORE than their own journey. It turns out that Blake has a very traumatizing past, and his experiences weren't lived through alone. In foster care, Blake had two foster brothers who became so much more than brothers. They united,bonded, and instead of living through the pain and despair on their own; they shared the burden of their troubles and developed an unbreakable bond that would last forever. The relationship between Blake, Cole, and Beckett intrigued me, and touched me so much that I was captivated by this unconventional trio.<br /><br />The three foster brothers play a big part in this story, in fact the book includes all of them. So not only is Poughskeepie about Blake and Livia, but about Cole and Beckett too. They add so much more to this tale, I feel that readers should know that this book is about six characters instead of two. It will not disappoint though, and I fell in love with both of them too. Well, I will be honest and say that Beckett stole a special corner of my heart. He is not your typical hero..he is a drug dealer,pimp, and murderer; but before you judge him..believe me he had his reasons and the biggest thing about Beckett is he protects the ones he loves. In this case, he would do anything for his brothers, and believe me he has.<br /><br />In addition to the bros..we get Kyle, who is Livia's sister...and I must say that she is friggin hilarious!!! She brings so much humor to this story; but don't let her fool you, as she too is suffering on the inside. In order not to feel her emotional pain, she tends to sleep around with any guy that will have her. She is very self destructive, and I can't help but think of a train wreck when I think of her. What happens though when Kyle lays her eyes on a handsome young man training to become a priest in the church? Cole is a kind soul, trying to follow the right path and put his past sins to rest. When these two troubled souls come together sparks fly; but nothing should come of it...after all..isn't Cole becoming a priest??? <br /><br />This is all just a brief taste of what you get in this action packed book. Expect to be highlighting a great deal of sentences because there is just so many profound words written by Debra Anastasia. This is an author who I think is brilliant, and I will be an avid follower after reading about Poughskeepie. <br />One big warning I will give about this book though, is basically -expect the unexpected. This isn't the most "realistic" story on the planet..but I overlooked that and just hopped along for the bumpiest ride of my life. I tried hard not to judge, and just went with how the circumstances made me feel. Also, Beckett is extremely protective over those he loves, and he will do things that most would not approve of. When you look beneath his surface though he is absolutely the kindnest soul of everyone, and it made me truly not want to think anything bad about him.. <br /><br />I highly recommend this story to anyone who likes a lot of drama, and just an all out fast paced book. One thing I hadn't expected was that this book had some dark spots in it. It isn't all flowery, fun and games..there is content in it that is disturbing and hard to swallow...Be prepared...but I will say that the darkness is worth it!!!<br /><br />Thank you to my Buddy's once again for a great read! Steph,Kelly,and Shanna; I always seem to enjoy my books way better when we have our group reads!!! I can't wait for the next one! Hugs ladies♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="10915719405029360107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_272539886" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272539886" />
    <a title="Mary B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3804735-mary-b"><img alt="Mary B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568428531p2/3804735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272539886?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary B." href="/user/show/3804735-mary-b">Mary B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13100412-poughkeepsie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=two-stars-or-less">two-stars-or-less</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=too-many-subplots-or-characters">too-many-subplots-or-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=romance-contemporary">romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=borrowed-from-kindle-friend">borrowed-from-kindle-friend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=entered-giveaway">entered-giveaway</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3804735-mary-b?shelf=tortured-past">tortured-past</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272539886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11469024443785180790">I was so disappointed. I was so excited to read this book because the subject was so unique. And for the first third to the first half of the book, I was enthralled. I loved it. Sure, it could be a tad melodramatic at times, but the arc was solid, the writing was good, and I loved the main characters - Livia and Blake. They were believable, and I was really looking forward to watching their romance play out and see them overcome whatever conflicts came their way. <br/><br/>Then somewhere about a third of </span>
  <span id="freeText11469024443785180790" style="display:none">I was so disappointed. I was so excited to read this book because the subject was so unique. And for the first third to the first half of the book, I was enthralled. I loved it. Sure, it could be a tad melodramatic at times, but the arc was solid, the writing was good, and I loved the main characters - Livia and Blake. They were believable, and I was really looking forward to watching their romance play out and see them overcome whatever conflicts came their way. <br /><br />Then somewhere about a third of the way through, the plot just collapsed. Completely and utterly. It became a complete mess of several different plot-lines, many of which had nothing to do with the supposed main characters, and none of which I cared about. It became way too difficult to follow. Secondary characters suddenly became primary, and we were introduced to the excruciatingly detailed, in-depth character histories of people who... I guess we were supposed to really care about...?.... But I didn't. This book just didn't know what it wanted to be, and it was trying desperately to be everything at once - and failing at all of it.<br /><br />I kept wondering 'What happened to this book?' Because at that point it ceased to feel like a book, and started to read more like scenes from a TV show that blends <i>The OC</i>, <i>Dawson's Creek</i>, and <i>Miami Vice</i>. WTF??<br /><br />Plus, the melodrama ramped up to epic proportions. It was very cheesy in parts, and very unrealistic. <br /><br />Such an enigma, because the second half of the book almost bears no resemblance to the first. <br /><br />The writing was good. Although, as I stated, a bit too detailed when it came to insignificant characters and inconsequential events. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11469024443785180790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_334102197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334102197" />
    <a title="J.m. Darhower" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1400656-j-m-darhower"><img alt="J.m. Darhower" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456272468p2/1400656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334102197?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.m. Darhower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.m. Darhower" href="/user/show/1400656-j-m-darhower">J.m. Darhower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334102197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7047146671457286851">Poughkeepsie, Poughkeepsie, Poughkeepsie... Oh, Poughkeepsie...<br/><br/>What do I say about you?<br/><br/>It took me awhile to finish this, only because people kept STEALING MY COPY. I've wanted to read it for a long time because I heard nothing but wonderful things, and Poughkeepsie certainly didn't disappoint. Blake's character tugged at my heart strings, him and Livia's relationship wholesome and sweet. It was hopeful, yet heartbreaking... certainly proves the point that you can't judge a book by its cover.<br/><br/>With</span>
  <span id="freeText7047146671457286851" style="display:none">Poughkeepsie, Poughkeepsie, Poughkeepsie... Oh, Poughkeepsie...<br /><br />What do I say about you?<br /><br />It took me awhile to finish this, only because people kept STEALING MY COPY. I've wanted to read it for a long time because I heard nothing but wonderful things, and Poughkeepsie certainly didn't disappoint. Blake's character tugged at my heart strings, him and Livia's relationship wholesome and sweet. It was hopeful, yet heartbreaking... certainly proves the point that you can't judge a book by its cover.<br /><br />Without a doubt, Beckett stole the show. I would kill for an entire Beckett book. I loved him and Eve's storyline. I won't give it away, but needless to say, I was a little stunned by their twist. Love it.<br /><br />Poughkeepsie is a long book but well worth the read. The end was a little too "wrapped up in a bow" for me, but that's just personal preference. I like open endedness, a little continued chaos with a not-so-happily ever after sometimes. But the ending was fitting for the characters.<br /><br />Very much looking forward to the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7047146671457286851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_233885517" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233885517" />
    <a title="Sandra " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5034547-sandra"><img alt="Sandra " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413920321p2/5034547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233885517?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra " href="/user/show/5034547-sandra">Sandra </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5034547-sandra?shelf=cry-me-a-river">cry-me-a-river</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5034547-sandra?shelf=flowers-and-chocolates">flowers-and-chocolates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5034547-sandra?shelf=angst-and-drama">angst-and-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5034547-sandra?shelf=rewritten-fanfiction">rewritten-fanfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5034547-sandra?shelf=read-the-fanfic-for-free">read-the-fanfic-for-free</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233885517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17657106985006384171"><i>Updated 10/9/12: I would like to point out that I read and reviewed this book in late 2011, upon its publication before the mass exodus of Twilight fanfics into publication as 'original' fiction. My opinion in regards to P2P has since changed and I no longer condone nor support the practice, no matter how much I loved the fanfic from where it came.</i><br/><br/>I have shelved this as rewritten fanfiction. I read the original fic online when it was Edward and Bella, and Jasper and Alice, and Emmett and Rosalie</span>
  <span id="freeText17657106985006384171" style="display:none"><i>Updated 10/9/12: I would like to point out that I read and reviewed this book in late 2011, upon its publication before the mass exodus of Twilight fanfics into publication as 'original' fiction. My opinion in regards to P2P has since changed and I no longer condone nor support the practice, no matter how much I loved the fanfic from where it came.</i><br /><br />I have shelved this as rewritten fanfiction. I read the original fic online when it was Edward and Bella, and Jasper and Alice, and Emmett and Rosalie. <br /><br />I loved it back then. <br /><br />When the author pulled it, I felt as if I had lost someone near and dear to my heart. <br /><br />When she announced that it was being reworked to be published, I waited patiently until that day came.<br /><br />And then I read it again. <br /><br />I love it now.<br /><br />This is essentially the same story, with a <u>lot of editing and tightening up and giving new names to the characters</u>, but the parts that captured my heart back then are all still within.<br /><br />At its heart, it's a love story between a homeless man and a strong, brave woman, a love story between a man lost in his delusion and invisible to the world and the woman who <i> sees him </i>. <br /><br />At its soul, it is way more than that. It's about friendship, redemption, loyalty, trust, family (be it blood-related or not) and, above all, the saving grace of love. <br /><br />Love never fails. Paul's first letter to the Corinthians tells us that, and I loved how the author used that well-known tidbit from the bible in her story. It may sound cliched to someone who hasn't read this story, but it feels to me as if the author took that letter from Paul, transferred it into modern times and wrote her story around it. <br /><br />Upon first opening the book, we are introduced to Livia McHugh, a college student who rides the train every morning from Poughkeepsie to the big city to attend her studies in psychology. She has a long-time boyfriend, and a smile for everyone who's waiting with her at the station, including the young, homeless man that everyone ignores and who lingers in the shadows by the station's platform. <br /><br />Blake Hartt watches Livia from afar and counts her smiles every day, knowing that he'll never be with a girl like her since he has nothing to offer. He's too proud to accept charity and too broken from the mistreatment by his late mother to find his way out of homelessness into a 'normal' life. It is enough for him to know that Livia truly <i> sees </i> him - and he is rewarded with her smile every morning, and every night when she returns home. <br /><br />Then one morning, a group of teenage boys accosts Blake with taunts and threats of violence. Livia is compelled to step between them, and getting them to leave Blake alone. He in turn is shocked but grateful that this young woman would come to his defense, and thus begins a friendship and then a love story that will make you laugh and cry and hug these characters to your chest, just to keep them safe. And at the end of the book, when you've followed their story all the way to its culmination, you feel as if you've been part of something amazing. <br /><br />Blake Hartt is a very interesting character. He was abused and mistreated by his alcoholic mother and entered the foster care system at age 12 due to an incident that leaves him feeling guilty and thinking that his skin is made of glass and would repel anyone who'd see him in the sun. After he aged out of the system, he has no place to go. He lives in the shadows until Livia's love gives him the strength to move into the sunlight and become the man he was always meant to be. He has impeccable manners, keeps himself clean with the help of his foster brother Cole's shower, but refuses to accept anything he deems unearned. You cannot help but fall in love with this man and his quiet, proud and thoughtful demeanor. <br /><br />We meet Cole and Beckett along the way, who lived in the same foster home as Blake, and upon aging out of the system, they remain brothers and do what they can to help each other. The way they go about it is as different as night and day.<br /><br />Beckett becomes a criminal, doing all the wrongs things for all the right reasons, all out of love for his brothers. Cole seeks the grace of God and is working as an assistant in a small, local church. <br /><br />We meet Kyle, Livia's younger sister, who took their mother's leaving them and turned it against herself, believing that she wasn't enough, that she isn't worth anything if her own mother can't love her. She is promiscuous, loud and can cuss up a storm. <br /><br />We meet Eve, who has lost her fiance and her baby due to a drive-by shooting and the resulting car accident. Eve is fueled by a need for revenge against the man who ordered the shooting until she is face-to-face with him and finds that she can't kill him. <br /><br />We meet John McHugh, father to Livia and Kyle, a cop, who loves his girls and only wants what's best for them. <br /><br />We meet a slew of minor characters, including Dr. Ted Hartt (yes, he shares a last name with Blake though I'll leave you to read to find out why) and Mouse aka Jimmy who serves as Beckett's bodyguard and whose role in this book is pivotal to the outcome.<br /><br />There are trials, misunderstandings, tribulations and setbacks, false starts and triumphs, there are moments when you want to reach into the book and shake a character into common sense, there are moments when your fist will form in your pocket because you want to hit someone who deserves it, there are moments when you fear and hold your breath, and there are moments when you cry and smile at the same time.<br /><br />Debra Anastasia takes you on a wild ride, have no doubt about it. <br /><br />A couple of things that might be construed as criticism:<br /><br />- the past tense of speed is sped. Not speeded. The proofreader in me cringed at that.<br />- the cursing. It's excessive when it comes to Beckett and a little innovative when it comes to Kyle. There were a few things that she uttered that sounded...weird, for lack of a better term. I don't know anyone who talks like that, but that's just me. Kyle's curses are something else. <br /><br />I particularly commend the author for really editing this story, really taking out the parts that weren't needed and thus tightening the narration and the story overall. <br /><br />Other than that, I must congratulate Ms. Anastasia for delivering a book that will stay with me for a long time, and one that I will re-read again and again. It's full of her own personal quirks, infused with laughter and tears, humor and seriousness, and above all overflows with the strength of pure love. <br /><br />I am honored and privileged to have been a part of this journey with you. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17657106985006384171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235441053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235441053" />
    <a title="Jennifer Lane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3574699-jennifer-lane"><img alt="Jennifer Lane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442497593p2/3574699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235441053?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Lane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Lane" href="/user/show/3574699-jennifer-lane">Jennifer Lane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=dysfunctional-family-fun">dysfunctional-family-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=omnific-publishing">omnific-publishing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=wounded-hero">wounded-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3574699-jennifer-lane?shelf=series">series</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235441053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11130867844743081071"><b>Deeply Touching</b><br/><br/>I've been wanting to read this story for some time due to the many elements that appeal to me: healing, redemption, crime, a psychology graduate student character (Livia), a homeless character (Blake), and a story full of emotion. Wow! I got all that and more.<br/><br/>Livia is one of the kindest people around. She smiles at everyone, including the quiet homeless man who frequents the shadows of the Poughkeepsie train station. One morning when some thugs threaten the man Livia's come to kno</span>
  <span id="freeText11130867844743081071" style="display:none"><b>Deeply Touching</b><br /><br />I've been wanting to read this story for some time due to the many elements that appeal to me: healing, redemption, crime, a psychology graduate student character (Livia), a homeless character (Blake), and a story full of emotion. Wow! I got all that and more.<br /><br />Livia is one of the kindest people around. She smiles at everyone, including the quiet homeless man who frequents the shadows of the Poughkeepsie train station. One morning when some thugs threaten the man Livia's come to known as "Green Eyes", Livia stands up for him. Their first words are adorable:<br /><br /><i>"You might want to find another place to sit," Livia said. "Those idiots could cook up a plan for revenge."<br />Instead of being the friendly advice Livia intended, her words seem to slice into him.<br />Why is he in such pain?<br />"I can't leave." Green Eyes took a huge breath. "This is the only place where I get to see you."</i><br /><br />I fell for the sensitive soul Blake from the start, especially after learning that he counts each of Livia's smiles. His foster brother Cole explains:<br /><br /><i>"He counts. You've smiled at him four hundred and forty-six times as of a few minutes ago."</i><br /><br />How cute is that?<br /><br />Blake might have a chance with Livia because her boyfriend Chris is a total <b>CAD</b>. I mean, he calls psychology "the study of psychos"! Grr.<br /><br />There are fantastic secondary characters in this novel:<br /><br />* Livia's younger sister Kyle. What a potty mouth! Blake says <i>"Pretty sure Kyle lacks any kind of editing mechanism"</i>. Their mother took off shortly after Kyle was born, and Kyle blames herself for not being worthy enough to make their mother stay. Kyle's low self-worth leads her to promiscuity. But perhaps she can find a love match in one of Blake's foster bros?<br /><br />* Cole is Blake's foster brother who's studying to be a priest. He has a violent past he's running from.<br /><br />* Beckett is a wildly colorful foster brother who aged out of the system before Cole and Blake, determined to pave the road for his brothers by committing all sorts of sins so they wouldn't have to. He's pretty much become a crime boss, with a muscled assistant named Mouse. Kyle refers to Beckett as "the human steroid." He doesn't believe in following rules, like parking in between the lines:<br /><br /><i>"I'm telling you, Cole, that's how it all gets started. The government's beating us down, and it all begins with those goddamn lines in the parking lot. Set yourself free, my brother. If you see a line, ignore it.</i><br /><br />Eve and Mouse were also wonderful characters, along with Livia and Kyle's police officer father.<br /><br />The flashbacks to the boys getting beaten by their foster dad, and the intensity between Beckett and Eve made me cry so hard.<br /><br />There are also so many freaking funny lines in the story, but I won't share all the off-color words here ha ha. But one chapter title "My Penis Rules the World" gives you a good flavor! And this excerpt when Kyle berates Livia and Blake at a religious ceremony is priceless (naughty language alert!)<br /><br /><i>"Will you get your asses up here? People are waiting. I mean Beckett here has maybe a few hours before he's bent over a metal toilet getting it up the ass from a guy named Bubba. Do you want him to have fun now or not?"<br />The streetlight illuminated Beckett as he appeared next to Kyle. "Why would I be the bitch? I don't think that's a fair f*cking assumption."<br />Kyle refused to look at him and crossed her arms. "Of course you'd be the bitch. You have dimples. Bitches have dimples. And I bet your ass is soft like two pillows."</i><br /><br />Debra, I love your screwballs sense of humor ;-) And I love even more that your story made me laugh and cry. An EXCELLENT read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11130867844743081071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1103847797" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103847797" />
    <a title="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9080319-allison-will-never-conquer-her-tbr"><img alt="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465384674p2/9080319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103847797?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" href="/user/show/9080319-allison-will-never-conquer-her-tbr">Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️</a>
